36. A transformer has a primary coil with 600 turns and a secondary coil with 200 turns. If the primary voltage is 240 V, what is the secondary voltage?
   A) 60 V
   B) 80 V
   C) 100 V
   D) 120 V

37. A capacitor with 30 µF is connected to a 120 V AC supply at 60 Hz. What is the capacitive reactance?
   A) 44 Ω
   B) 88 Ω
   C) 177 Ω
   D) 265 Ω

38. A 20 µF capacitor is charged to 100 V. How much energy is stored in the capacitor?
   A) 0.1 J
   B) 0.2 J
   C) 0.5 J
   D) 1 J

39. What is the wavelength of an electromagnetic wave with a frequency of 500 MHz in a vacuum?
   A) 0.6 m
   B) 0.5 m
   C) 0.4 m
   D) 0.3 m

40. A 50 m copper wire has a cross-sectional area of 2 mm² and a resistivity of 1.7×10⁻⁸ Ω·m. What is its resistance?
   A) 0.42 Ω
   B) 0.85 Ω
   C) 1.25 Ω
   D) 2.5 Ω



--- CORRECT ANSWERS AND EXPLANATIONS ---

1. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: The total resistance in the circuit is 10 + 5 = 15 ohms. Using Ohm's law (V = IR), the current is I = V / R = 20 / 15 = 1.33 A.

2. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: The induced EMF can be calculated using Faraday's Law: EMF = -N * ΔΦ / Δt. Here, N = 500, ΔΦ = 0.3 - 0.1 = 0.2 Wb, Δt = 2 s. EMF = -500 * 0.2 / 2 = -50 V. The magnitude is 50 V.

3. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: Apparent power S (VA) is calculated as S = P / pf, where P = 900 W and pf = 0.8. S = 900 / 0.8 = 1125 VA.

4. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: The magnetic flux density B = μ₀ * μr * H, where μ₀ = 4π x 10⁻⁷ Tm/A, μr = 1000, and H = 2000 A/m. B = (4π x 10⁻⁷) * 1000 * 2000 = 4 T.

5. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: In parallel, the total capacitance is C = C₁ + C₂ = 10 + 20 = 30 µF. The charge Q = C * V = 30 * 50 = 1500 µC.

6. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: Inductive reactance Xₗ = 2πfL, where f = 60 Hz and L = 10 mH = 0.01 H. Xₗ = 2π * 60 * 0.01 = 6.28 Ω.

7. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: Using Coulomb's law: F = k * |Q₁Q₂| / r², where k = 9 x 10⁹ Nm²/C², Q₁ = 3 x 10⁻⁶ C, Q₂ = -2 x 10⁻⁶ C, and r = 0.5 m. F = 9 x 10⁹ * (3 x 10⁻⁶ * 2 x 10⁻⁶) / 0.5² = 0.216 N.

8. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Energy stored in a capacitor is given by E = 0.5 * C * V². Here, C = 5 x 10⁻⁶ F and V = 50 V. E = 0.5 * 5 x 10⁻⁶ * 50² = 12.5 mJ.

9. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: The temperature coefficient α = (R₂ - R₁) / [R₁ * (T₂ - T₁)]. R₁ = 5 Ω, R₂ = 7 Ω, T₁ = 20°C, T₂ = 60°C. α = (7 - 5) / [5 * (60 - 20)] = 0.01 Ω/°C.

10. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: Using the transformer voltage ratio: V₂ / V₁ = N₂ / N₁. V₂ = V₁ * (N₂ / N₁) = 240 * (100 / 400) = 60 V.

11. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: The total resistance of the parallel combination is calculated as 1/R_total = 1/15 + 1/10, resulting in R_total = 6 ohms. The total current is then I = V/R_total = 30/6 = 5.0 A. This current divides according to the resistances, giving approximately 4.5 A through the 10-ohm resistor.

12. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: The magnetic field inside a solenoid is calculated using B = µ₀ * n * I, where n = number of turns/length = 800/0.5 = 1600 turns/m, µ₀ = 4π × 10⁻⁷ T·m/A. Substituting values gives B = 4π × 10⁻⁷ × 1600 × 3 ≈ 0.024 T.

13. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Using Coulomb's law: F = k * |Q₁ * Q₂| / r², where k = 9 × 10⁹ N·m²/C². Substituting values, F = 9 × 10⁹ × (6 × 10⁻⁶ × 4 × 10⁻⁶) / 0.3² ≈ 4.8 N.

14. Correct Answer: D
   Explanation: Impedance in a series circuit is calculated as Z = √(R² + Xₗ²). Here, R = 10 Ω and Xₗ = 15 Ω, so Z = √(10² + 15²) = √(100 + 225) = √325 ≈ 18 Ω.

15. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: From Faraday's law, EMF = -ΔΦ / Δt. Magnetic flux Φ = B * A, where A = π * r² = π * (0.1)² ≈ 0.0314 m². ΔΦ = Φ_initial - Φ_final = 0.5 * 0.0314 - 0 = 0.0157. EMF = -ΔΦ / Δt = -0.0157 / 0.2 = 0.1 V.

16. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: Input electrical power = V * I = 120 * 8 = 960 W. Mechanical power output = efficiency * input power = 0.85 * 960 ≈ 816 W.

17. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Electric field E = k * Q / r², where k = 9 × 10⁹ N·m²/C². Substituting, E = 9 × 10⁹ × 10 × 10⁻⁶ / 0.2² = 4.50 × 10⁵ N/C.

18. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: Capacitive reactance X_c = 1 / (2πfC). Substituting, X_c = 1 / (2π × 60 × 50 × 10⁻⁶) ≈ 53 Ω.

19. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: In a parallel circuit, the total resistance is calculated as 1/R_total = 1/R₁ + 1/R₂ + 1/R₃. Total resistance = 1/(1/2 + 1/4 + 1/6) = 1 Ω. Current supplied is I = V/R = 12/1 = 12 A.

20. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: Induced EMF is calculated using Faraday's law: EMF = -N * (ΔΦ/Δt). ΔΦ = B * Area. EMF = -200 * ((0.2 - 0.05) * 0.1/0.02) = 15 V.

21. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: The magnetic field inside a solenoid is given by B = μ₀ * (N/L) * I. B = (4π × 10⁻⁷) * (1000/1) * 5 = 0.0055 T.

22. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: In a series connection, Q is constant. V₁/V₂ = C₂/C₁. Total voltage = 100 V, Voltage across 10 µF = C₁/(C₁ + C₂) * Total Voltage = 5/(5+10) * 100 = 66.7 V.

23. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: Force is calculated using Coulomb's law: F = k * |q₁*q₂|/r². F = (9 × 10⁹) * (5 × 10⁻⁶ * -3 × 10⁻⁶)/(0.4)² = 3.375 N.

24. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: Impedance Z = √(R² + Xₗ²). Xₗ = ωL = 2πfL. Xₗ = 2π * 50 * 0.02 = 6.28 Ω. Z = √(10² + 6.28²) = 14.56 Ω.

25. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: The voltage ratio is given by V₁/V₂ = N₁/N₂. Secondary voltage = (N₂/N₁) * V₁ = (200/500) * 240 = 96 V.

26. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Wavelength λ = c/f. λ = (3 × 10⁸)/(300 × 10⁶) = 1 m.

27. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: Power dissipated is P = I²R. P = 5² * 2 = 25 W.

28. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: B = μ₀ * μᵣ * H. H = B/(μ₀ * μᵣ). H = 0.1/(4π × 10⁻⁷ * 2000) ≈ 100 A/m.

29. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: The total resistance of the circuit is R = 12 Ω + 4 Ω = 16 Ω. Using Ohm's law, I = V/R = 24 V / 16 Ω = 1 A.

30. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: The induced EMF is calculated using Faraday's Law: EMF = -N × (ΔΦ/Δt). ΔΦ = B × A = (0.2 - 0.05) × 0.1 = 0.015 Wb. EMF = -300 × (0.015 / 0.01) = 1.5 V.

31. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: The total power in a three-phase system is P = √3 × V × I × PF. P = √3 × 400 × 10 × 0.9 = 4.8 kW.

32. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: In series, the equivalent capacitance is C_eq = (C₁ × C₂) / (C₁ + C₂) = (6×12)/(6+12) = 4 µF. Voltage across C₁ is V₁ = Q / C₁. Since Q = C_eq × V, Q = 4×100 = 400 µC. V₁ = 400 / 6 = 75 V.

33. Correct Answer: D
   Explanation: Magnetic field strength inside a solenoid is B = µ₀ × n × I. n = N/l = 500/0.4 = 1250 turns/m. B = (4π×10⁻⁷) × 1250 × 8 = 0.08 T.

34. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Force is given by Coulomb's Law: F = k × |Q₁ × Q₂| / r². k = 9 × 10⁹ N·m²/C². F = (9×10⁹) × (5×10⁻⁶ × 3×10⁻⁶) / 0.6² = 0.625 N.

35. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: Impedance Z = √(R² + Xₗ²). Xₗ = 2πfL = 2π×50×0.03 = 9.42 Ω. Z = √(15² + 9.42²) = √(225 + 88.8) = 24 Ω.

36. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: The voltage ratio is given by V₂/V₁ = N₂/N₁. V₂ = V₁ × (N₂/N₁) = 240 × (200/600) = 80 V.

37. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Capacitive reactance X_c = 1/(2πfC). X_c = 1/(2×π×60×30×10⁻⁶) = 88 Ω.

38. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: Energy stored in a capacitor is U = 0.5×C×V². U = 0.5 × 20×10⁻⁶ × 100² = 0.5 J.

39. Correct Answer: D
   Explanation: Wavelength λ = c/f. c = 3×10⁸ m/s. λ = (3×10⁸)/(500×10⁶) = 0.3 m.

40. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: Resistance R = ρL/A. R = (1.7×10⁻⁸ × 50) / (2×10⁻⁶) = 0.42 Ω.

FE MECHANICAL – Statics

1. A beam of length 10 m is supported at both ends and carries a uniform distributed load of 4 kN/m. What is the reaction force at each support?
   A) 10 kN
   B) 20 kN
   C) 40 kN
   D) 50 kN

2. In a simple truss, what is the force in member AB given that the structure is symmetrical and the load at the center joint is 5 kN?
   A) 2.5 kN in tension
   B) 5 kN in tension
   C) 2.5 kN in compression
   D) 5 kN in compression

3. Find the centroid of a triangular plate with a base of 6 m and a height of 9 m.
   A) (2 m, 3 m)
   B) (3 m, 6 m)
   C) (2 m, 6 m)
   D) (3 m, 3 m)

4. A 200 N force is applied at a distance of 3 m from the pivot point. Calculate the moment generated by this force.
   A) 600 Nm
   B) 400 Nm
   C) 200 Nm
   D) 1000 Nm

5. A block weighing 50 N rests on a horizontal surface with a coefficient of friction of 0.4. What is the maximum force that can be applied horizontally before the block starts moving?
   A) 20 N
   B) 25 N
   C) 30 N
   D) 35 N

6. A ladder weighing 100 N is leaning against a wall at an angle of 60 degrees. If the wall is frictionless, what is the reaction force at the ground?
   A) 50 N
   B) 100 N
   C) 150 N
   D) 200 N

7. For a beam subjected to both a concentrated load of 10 kN and a uniformly distributed load of 5 kN/m over its 4 m length, what is the total downward force acting on the beam?
   A) 20 kN
   B) 30 kN
   C) 40 kN
   D) 50 kN

8. A disk of radius 0.5 m and mass 10 kg is subjected to a torque of 25 Nm. What is its angular acceleration?
   A) 1 rad/s²
   B) 2.5 rad/s²
   C) 5 rad/s²
   D) 10 rad/s²

9. Calculate the shear force at the midpoint of a simply supported beam carrying a point load of 15 kN at the center and a total length of 10 m.
   A) 7.5 kN
   B) 15 kN
   C) 22.5 kN
   D) 0 kN

10. A beam of length 5 m carries a distributed load varying linearly from 0 to 10 kN/m. What is the total load acting on the beam?
   A) 25 kN
   B) 50 kN
   C) 75 kN
   D) 100 kN

11. A 10 kg box is resting on a flat surface. A 50 N force is applied horizontally to the box, and the coefficient of static friction between the box and the surface is 0.4. What is the frictional force acting on the box?
   A) 40 N
   B) 50 N
   C) 0 N
   D) 10 N

12. A uniform beam of length 6 m and weight 300 N is supported at its ends. A 200 N load is applied at 2 m from one end. What is the reaction force at the support closest to the load?
   A) 200 N
   B) 300 N
   C) 400 N
   D) 100 N

   A) 115.47 N
   B) 86.60 N
   C) 130.00 N
   D) 100.00 N

   B) (2 m, 1.5 m)
   C) (2.2 m, 1.7 m)
   D) (1.9 m, 1.5 m)

   B) 5094 N

99. A dam gate of height 4 m and width 3 m holds back water. The top of the gate is at the water surface. What is the hydrostatic force on the gate?
   A) 24 kN
   B) 48 kN
   C) 72 kN
   D) 96 kN

100. A rope is pulling a box of 200 N horizontally across a rough surface with an angle of inclination of 30°. The coefficient of kinetic friction is 0.4. What is the tension in the rope if the box moves at constant velocity?
   A) 80 N
   B) 160 N
   C) 200 N
   D) 240 N



--- CORRECT ANSWERS AND EXPLANATIONS ---

1. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: The total load on the beam is 4 kN/m × 10 m = 40 kN. Since the beam is symmetrically supported, each support carries half the total load. Thus, the reaction at each support is 40 kN ÷ 2 = 20 kN.

2. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: Using the method of joints, the force in member AB can be calculated as half the total load (5 kN) distributed equally due to symmetry. The member experiences tension as it is stretching away from the joint.

3. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: The centroid of a triangular area is located at 1/3 the height from the base and 1/3 the base length from the vertex. Hence, the coordinates are (1/3 × 6, 1/3 × 9) = (3 m, 6 m).

4. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: Moment is calculated as force × distance. Here, moment = 200 N × 3 m = 600 Nm.

5. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: The maximum force before motion is determined by F_friction = μ × N, where μ is the coefficient of friction and N is the normal force. F_friction = 0.4 × 50 N = 20 N.

6. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Since the wall is frictionless, the vertical component of forces must balance with the weight of the ladder. The reaction force at the ground equals the ladder’s weight, which is 100 N.

7. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: The total downward force is the sum of the concentrated load and the distributed load. Total load = 10 kN + (5 kN/m × 4 m) = 10 kN + 20 kN = 40 kN.

8. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Using the formula Torque = I × α, where I is the moment of inertia of a disk (I = 0.5 × m × r²), I = 0.5 × 10 × 0.5² = 1.25 kg·m². Torque = 25 Nm, so angular acceleration α = Torque/I = 25/1.25 = 2.5 rad/s².

9. Correct Answer: D
   Explanation: At the midpoint where the point load is applied, the shear force changes direction. Hence, the shear force at the midpoint is zero.

10. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: For a triangular distributed load, the total load is equal to the area under the load curve: (1/2 × base × height). Total load = 1/2 × 5 × 10 = 25 kN.

11. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: The maximum static friction is calculated using f_max = μ × Normal Force = 0.4 × (10 kg × 9.81 m/s²) = 40 N. Since the applied force is less than the maximum static friction, the frictional force equals the applied force, which is 40 N.

12. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: Using sum of moments about the far support, Reaction Force = (200 N × 2 m + 300 N × 3 m + Beam weight's center at 3 m from closest support) / 6 m. Solving gives 400 N.

13. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: Resolving forces into components and using equilibrium equations: Force in member AB = √(100² + 50²) = 115.47 N.

14. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Calculate the centroid of both shapes weighted by their areas and masses. Rectangle’s centroid at (1.5, 1); Triangle's centroid at (2, 0.67). Combine weighted averages for composite.

15. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Maximum friction force is f_max = μ × Normal Force; Normal Force = (1200 × 9.81) × cos(30°), f_max = 0.5 × Normal Force = 5094 N.

16. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: Moment at center = Load × Distance to center × (distance / 2). Uniform load is symmetrical, moment = 100 N/m × 5 m × (5/2) ÷ 2 = 125 N·m.

17. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Stress = Force / Area. Stress = 10 kN / 0.02 m² = 0.5 MPa. Ensure units are consistent for calculation.

18. Correct Answer: D
   Explanation: Stress = Force / Area. Stress = 500 N / 0.01 m² = 5 MPa. Always check units for consistency.

19. Correct Answer: D
   Explanation: From equilibrium conditions, Horizontal force from wall = Ladder weight × tan(60°) / 2 = 173 N.

20. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: Torque = Force × Radius; Force = Torque / Radius = 30 N·m / 0.3 m = 90 N.

21. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: Using the equations of equilibrium, the sum of vertical forces and moments can be calculated to find the reaction forces. At the left support, the moment equation gives R1 = (500 * 3) / 8 = 375 N.

22. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: The angle can be calculated using trigonometry: tan(θ) = vertical load / horizontal tension. θ = arctan(200/400) = 26.57°.

23. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: The center of gravity of a triangular plate is located at 1/3 the height from the base and 1/3 the base length from the vertex.

24. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: Using the Pythagorean theorem: Resultant = √(100² + 150²) = √(10000 + 22500) = √32500 = 180.28 N.

25. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: Using the principle of moments: Force * 1 = 300 * 0.5. Force = 150 N.

26. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: Taking moments about the hinge: Tension * sin(45) * 4 = 200 * 2. Solving for Tension, T = (400 / 2) / 0.707 = 282.84 N.

27. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: For equilibrium, F = √(200² + 300²) = √(40000 + 90000) = √130000 = 360.56 N.

28. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Hydrostatic force = Pressure * Area. Pressure = ρgh = 1000 * 9.81 * 5. Area = πr² = π * 2². Force = (1000 * 9.81 * 5) * (π * 4) = 125.6 kN.

29. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: The total load is the area under the load distribution curve, which is a triangle. Area = 0.5 * base * height = 0.5 * 10 * 100 = 500 N.

30. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Stress = Force / Area. Stress = 10,000 N / (100 × 10⁻⁶ m²) = 100 × 10⁶ Pa = 100 MPa.

31. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: Using the equilibrium equations ΣFx = 0, ΣFy = 0, and ΣM = 0, calculate the reactions at the supports. Taking moments about the right support, the reaction at the left support is 200 N, and the reaction at the right support is 100 N.

32. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Using the method of joints, analyze joint B. Resolve the vertical and horizontal force components to determine the force in AB. It is 400 N in tension.

33. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: Bending moment at the fixed end equals the total load (w × L) multiplied by the distance to the centroid of the load (L/2). This gives 200 × 5 × (5/2) = 2500 N·m.

34. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: The maximum force is given by the static friction force, F = μN, where N = weight × cos(30°). Calculate N and substitute μ = 0.4 to find F.

35. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: For a cantilever beam with a point load at the free end, the deflection at the free end is given by δ = PL³/(3EI).

36. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: Resolve forces horizontally and vertically. Using the angles provided, solve the system of equilibrium equations to determine the tension in Cable 1.

37. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: The moment of inertia of a solid disk about its central axis is I = (1/2)MR². Use the given weight to calculate mass (M = W/g) and substitute into the formula.

38. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: The center of gravity of a uniform rectangular plate is located at its geometric center, which is at half the length and half the width.

39. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Shear stress is τ = T*r/J, where J = πr⁴/2 for a solid circular cross-section. Substituting torque and radius gives τ = 10,000 N/m².

40. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: The total load for a triangular distributed load is given by (1/2) × base × height. Substituting base = 8 m and height = 400 N/m gives 1600 N.

41. Correct Answer: D
   Explanation: The reaction at the right support is found by summing moments about the left support. Using the moment equilibrium equation, R2 * 5 = (400 * 2) + (600 * 4). Solving for R2 gives R2 = 800 N.

42. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: The horizontal reaction force is equal to the horizontal component of the force exerted by the wall. Using moment equilibrium about the base, the horizontal reaction force is R_H = 500 N * tan(60°) = 433 N.

43. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: By summing moments about the hinge, the tension in the cable is calculated as Tension = 200 N × (1.5 m) / (sin(45°) × 3 m). Solving this gives a tension of 282.8 N.

44. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: Using equilibrium, the vertical components of the tensions add up to the weight of the crate. T1 sin(30°) + T2 sin(60°) = 150 N. Since T1 cos(30°) = T2 cos(60°), solving the system gives T1 = 173.2 N.

45. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: The tension in the cable must equal the weight of the plate since the hinge provides no vertical reaction force in this configuration. Thus, Tension = 300 N.

   Explanation: The moment at the fixed end is due to the point load at the free end. Moment = Force × Distance = 400 N × 5 m = 2000 N·m.

47. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: The resultant force is calculated using the law of cosines: R = √(200² + 300² - 2 × 200 × 300 × cos(120°)) = 346 N.

48. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Torque is the product of tangential force and radius. Torque = 50 N × 1 m = 50 N·m.

49. Correct Answer: D
   Explanation: The total load is 200 N/m × 8 m = 1600 N. Each support shares half of the total load, so the reaction force at each support is 1600 N ÷ 2 = 800 N.

50. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: The horizontal tension in the cable (T) can be found using T = 500 / (2 × 0.5 / 5), which simplifies to 2500 N.

51. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: The total distributed load is 2 kN/m × 10 m = 20 kN. Since the beam is symmetrically loaded, each support will carry half the load: 20 kN / 2 = 10 kN.

   Explanation: The reaction force at the base must counteract both the vertical weight and any horizontal forces. Using trigonometry, the vertical reaction is 200 N, and horizontal forces depend on the smooth wall interaction.

53. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: Moment is calculated as force × distance. Thus, the moment = 500 N × 3 m = 1500 N·m.

   Explanation: For a planar truss, the number of members (m) must equal 2j - 3, where j is the number of joints, to ensure static determinacy.

55. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: The resultant force can be found using the Pythagorean theorem: √(300² + 400²) = √(90000 + 160000) = √250000 = 500 N.

FE MECHANICAL – Dynamics, Kinematics, and Vibrations

1. A 5 kg block is placed on a smooth horizontal surface and is acted upon by a force of 20 N. What is the acceleration of the block?
   A) 4 m/s²
   B) 5 m/s²
   C) 2 m/s²
   D) 3 m/s²

2. A ball is thrown vertically upward with an initial velocity of 15 m/s. Ignoring air resistance, how long will it take for the ball to reach its highest point?
   A) 1.5 seconds
   B) 2.5 seconds
   C) 3.0 seconds
   D) 4.0 seconds

3. A mass-spring system has a natural frequency of 5 Hz. If the mass is doubled, what will be the new natural frequency?
   A) 2.5 Hz
   B) 3.5 Hz
   C) 5 Hz
   D) 7 Hz

4. A car traveling at 20 m/s decelerates uniformly at a rate of 2 m/s². How far does it travel before coming to a stop?
   A) 100 m
   B) 200 m
   C) 300 m
   D) 400 m

5. A projectile is launched at an angle of 45° with a velocity of 20 m/s. What is the maximum height it reaches?
   A) 10 m
   B) 15 m
   C) 20 m
   D) 25 m

6. A 3 kg mass attached to a spring oscillates with a period of 2 seconds. What is the spring constant?
   A) 15 N/m
   B) 30 N/m
   C) 45 N/m
   D) 60 N/m

7. A 50 kg crate is pushed across a rough surface with a coefficient of kinetic friction of 0.3. What is the frictional force acting on the crate?
   A) 150 N
   B) 200 N
   C) 300 N
   D) 500 N

8. An object moves with constant acceleration. If its initial velocity is 5 m/s and acceleration is 3 m/s², what is its velocity after 4 seconds?
   A) 17 m/s
   B) 18 m/s

120. A train moving at 25 m/s decelerates uniformly to a stop in 20 seconds. What distance does the train travel during this time?
   A) 500 m
   B) 300 m
   C) 250 m
   D) 100 m



--- CORRECT ANSWERS AND EXPLANATIONS ---

1. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: Using Newton's Second Law, F = ma. Acceleration (a) = Force (F) / Mass (m). Thus, a = 20 N / 5 kg = 4 m/s².

2. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: At the highest point, velocity is zero. Using v = u + at, where v = 0, u = 15 m/s, and g = -9.8 m/s², the time to reach the highest point is t = u / g = 15 / 9.8 ≈ 1.5 seconds.

3. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: The natural frequency is proportional to the square root of (1 / mass). Doubling the mass reduces the frequency to √(1/2) of the original, or 5 Hz * √(1/2) ≈ 2.5 Hz.

4. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: Using the equation v² = u² + 2as, where v = 0, u = 20 m/s, a = -2 m/s², solve for s: s = u² / (2|a|) = 20² / (2 * 2) = 100 m.

5. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Vertical velocity component = u * sin(θ) = 20 * sin(45°) ≈ 14.14 m/s. Maximum height = (v²) / (2g) = (14.14²) / (2 * 9.8) ≈ 15 m.

6. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: The period T = 2π√(m/k). Rearrange to find k: k = (4π²m) / T². Substituting m = 3 kg and T = 2 s gives k ≈ 30 N/m.

7. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: Frictional force is given by F = μ * m * g. Substituting μ = 0.3, m = 50 kg, and g = 9.8 m/s² gives F = 0.3 * 50 * 9.8 ≈ 150 N.

8. Correct Answer: D
   Explanation: Using v = u + at, v = 5 + (3 * 4) = 20 m/s.

9. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: The damping ratio is the percentage reduction in amplitude per cycle, hence 20% corresponds to a damping ratio of 0.2.

10. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: The period of a pendulum for small oscillations is T = 2π√(L/g). Substituting L = 2 m and g = 9.8 m/s² gives T ≈ 2.83 s.

11. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Using s = ut + 0.5at², where u = 0, a = 4 m/s², t = 5 s: s = 0.5 * 4 * 5² = 60 m.

12. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: The total energy is the sum of potential and kinetic energy. Maximum kinetic energy = Total energy - Maximum potential energy = 50 J - 30 J = 20 J.

13. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: The acceleration down the incline is given by g*sin(θ). Substituting g = 9.8 m/s² and θ = 30°, acceleration = 9.8*sin(30°) = 4.9 m/s².

14. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Using the formula a = (vf - vi)/t, where vf = 20 m/s, vi = 0 m/s, and t = 10 s, the acceleration is (20 - 0)/10 = 2 m/s².

15. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: The period of a simple pendulum is given by T = 2π√(L/g). Substituting L = 2 m and g = 9.8 m/s², T = 2π√(2/9.8) ≈ 3.14 s.

16. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: Using Newton's second law, F = ma, rearranging gives a = F/m. Substituting F = 15 N and m = 5 kg, a = 15/5 = 3 m/s².

17. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: Using the formula h = v²/(2g), where v = 25 m/s and g = 9.8 m/s², the height is h = (25)² / (2 * 9.8) = 31.25 m.

18. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: The natural frequency is given by f = (1/2π)√(k/m). Substituting k = 50 N/m and m = 2 kg, f = (1/2π)√(50/2) ≈ 1.59 Hz.

19. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Using the formula ω = ω₀ + αt, where ω₀ = 10 rad/s, α = 2 rad/s², and t = 3 s, ω = 10 + 2*3 = 16 rad/s.

   Explanation: The vertical velocity is v*sin(45°). Using h = v²/(2g), where g = 9.8 m/s², calculate maximum height using components.

23. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: The net force is F_net = Applied force - Friction force. Friction force is calculated as f_k = μ_k * (m * g). Plugging in values, F_net = 100 - (0.3 * 15 * 9.81) ≈ 55.9 N. Using F_net = m * a, we find a ≈ 55.9 / 15 ≈ 4.4 m/s².

FE MECHANICAL – Mechanics of Materials

1. A steel rod with a length of 2 meters and a diameter of 10 mm is subjected to a tensile force of 20 kN. Calculate the normal stress in the rod. Assume the rod is uniform throughout its length.
   A) 127.4 MPa
   B) 254.6 MPa
   C) 318.3 MPa
   D) 400.0 MPa

2. A rectangular beam with a width of 100 mm and a height of 200 mm is subjected to a shear force of 10 kN. Determine the maximum shear stress in the beam.
   A) 1.25 MPa
   B) 0.75 MPa
   C) 0.833 MPa
   D) 1.67 MPa

3. A simply supported beam with a span of 4 meters is subjected to a point load of 5 kN at its mid-span. If the cross-section is a rectangle with a width of 150 mm and a height of 250 mm, what is the maximum bending stress in the beam?
   A) 9.6 MPa
   B) 11.2 MPa
   C) 16.0 MPa
   D) 19.2 MPa

4. A cantilever beam with a length of 3 meters is subjected to a uniformly distributed load of 2 kN/m. What is the maximum deflection of the beam? Assume E = 200 GPa and I = 4 × 10^-6 m⁴.
   A) 3.38 mm
   B) 4.50 mm
   C) 5.06 mm
   D) 6.75 mm

5. A steel bar with a length of 1.5 meters is constrained at both ends. If the temperature increases by 50°C, what is the thermal stress developed in the bar? Assume α = 12 × 10^-6/°C and E = 200 GPa.
   A) 60 MPa
   B) 120 MPa
   C) 180 MPa
   D) 240 MPa

6. A solid circular shaft with a diameter of 50 mm is subjected to a torque of 200 Nm. Calculate the shear stress at the outer surface of the shaft.
   A) 16.28 MPa
   B) 20.37 MPa
   C) 25.47 MPa
   D) 30.89 MPa

7. A state of stress at a point in a material is given as σ_x = 50 MPa, σ_y = 30 MPa, and τ_xy = 20 MPa. Calculate the maximum shear stress using Mohr’s Circle.

98. A cantilever beam of length 3 m is subjected to a uniformly distributed load of 2 kN/m. Find the deflection at the free end.

   D) 20 mm

99. A rectangular steel beam with a width of 100 mm and height of 200 mm is subjected to a bending moment of 50 kNm. Calculate the maximum bending stress in the beam.
   A) 12.5 MPa
   B) 25 MPa
   C) 50 MPa
   D) 100 MPa

100. Determine the critical buckling load for a steel column with a length of 3 m, fixed at both ends, and a moment of inertia of 80 × 10⁶ mm⁴. The modulus of elasticity is 200 GPa.
   A) 822 kN
   B) 1000 kN
   C) 655 kN
   D) 500 kN




--- CORRECT ANSWERS AND EXPLANATIONS ---

1. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: Normal stress is given by σ = F/A. The cross-sectional area A = π/4 × d² = π/4 × (0.01)² = 7.854 × 10^-5 m². The stress is σ = 20000 / (7.854 × 10^-5) = 127.4 MPa.

2. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: The maximum shear stress in a rectangular cross-section is τ_max = 1.5 × V/A. Here, A = b × h = 0.1 × 0.2 = 0.02 m². τ_max = 1.5 × 10000 / 0.02 = 0.833 MPa.

3. Correct Answer: D
   Explanation: The maximum bending stress is given by σ = M*c/I. Moment M = (P*L)/4 = (5000×4)/4 = 5000 Nm. I = (b*h³)/12 = (0.15×(0.25)³)/12 = 1.953×10^-4 m⁴. c = h/2 = 0.125 m. Therefore, σ = 5000×0.125 / 1.953×10^-4 = 19.2 MPa.

4. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: The maximum deflection for a cantilever beam under UDL is δ = (w*L⁴)/(8*E*I). Substituting, δ = (2000*3⁴)/(8×200×10⁹×4×10^-6) = 0.00338 m = 3.38 mm.

5. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Thermal stress is σ = α*E*ΔT. Substituting, σ = 12×10^-6×200×10⁹×50 = 120 MPa.

6. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: The shear stress is given by τ = T*r/J. J = π/32*d⁴ = π/32*(0.05)⁴ = 3.068×10^-6 m⁴. r = d/2 = 0.025 m. τ = 200×0.025 / 3.068×10^-6 = 20.37 MPa.

7. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: Max shear stress is τ_max = √[((σ_x - σ_y)/2)² + τ_xy²]. Substituting, τ_max = √[((50-30)/2)² + 20²] = 25 MPa.

8. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Principal stresses are given by σ₁,₂ = [(σ_x + σ_y)/2] ± √[((σ_x - σ_y)/2)² + τ_xy²]. Substituting, σ₁ = 55 MPa and σ₂ = 5 MPa.

9. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: The bending stress is given by σ = M*c/I. Substituting, σ = 10000×0.1 / 8×10^-6 = 125 MPa.

10. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Hoop stress is given by σ_h = (p*r)/t. Substituting, σ_h = 1×10⁶×0.5 / 0.01 = 100 MPa.

   Explanation: Normal stress is calculated using the formula σ = F/A. Substituting the values: σ = 50,000 N / 25 × 10^-6 m² = 100 MPa.

25. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Von Mises stress is calculated as √(σ₁² + σ₂² - σ₁σ₂ + 3τ²).

   Explanation: Critical load is calculated using P_cr = (π²EI)/(K*L)², where K is the effective length factor.

   Explanation: Thermal stress is calculated as σ = α*E*ΔT.

28. Correct Answer: D
   Explanation: Hoop stress is calculated as σ_h = (p*r)/t.

29. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Maximum shear stress is calculated as τ_max = √[((σ_x - σ_y)/2)² + τ_xy²].

30. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: At the fixed support, the bending moment is equal to the load multiplied by the beam length.

31. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: Stress amplitude is calculated as (σ_max - σ_min)/2.

32. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Factor of safety is calculated as yield strength / working stress.

33. Correct Answer: B

36. Correct Answer: A

FE MECHANICAL – Material Properties and Processing

1. Which material property is most critical for preventing permanent deformation under load?
   A) Elastic modulus
   B) Yield strength
   C) Hardness
   D) Thermal conductivity

2. During heat treatment of steel, which process improves hardness by cooling rapidly after heating?
   A) Annealing
   B) Quenching
   C) Normalizing
   D) Tempering

3. What does the term 'creep' refer to in material science?
   A) Abrupt failure due to fatigue
   B) Slow deformation under sustained load
   C) Fracture due to excessive strain
   D) Resistance to wear during motion

4. Which material processing technique involves the removal of impurities from molten metal?
   A) Casting
   B) Alloying
   C) Refining
   D) Extrusion

5. A ductile material is defined by its ability to:
   A) Absorb energy without fracturing
   B) Undergo significant plastic deformation before failure
   C) Resist surface wear and abrasion
   D) Conduct electricity efficiently

6. Which manufacturing process is used to produce components with high dimensional accuracy by removing material?
   A) Forging
   B) Casting
   C) Machining
   D) Extrusion

7. Which of the following materials exhibits the highest tensile strength?
   A) Aluminum
   B) Steel
   C) Copper
   D) Polymer-based composites

8. In metal forming, which process involves compressing a workpiece between two dies to shape it?
   A) Forging
   B) Rolling
   C) Extrusion
   D) Casting

9. Which test is used to determine the impact strength of a material?
   A) Charpy test
   B) Tensile test
   C) Hardness test
   D) Fatigue test

10. Which welding method produces the highest strength welds for structural applications?
   A) Arc welding
   B) Friction stir welding
   C) Gas welding
   D) Laser beam welding

11. Which factor influences the fatigue life of a material the most?
   A) Surface roughness
   B) Thermal conductivity
   C) Electrical resistance
   D) Density

12. Which process involves heating and cooling a material to relieve internal stresses without altering its microstructure?
   A) Annealing
   B) Stress relieving
   C) Quenching
   D) Carburizing

13. What type of material typically exhibits viscoelastic behavior?
   A) Metals
   B) Ceramics
   C) Polymers
   D) Composites

14. Which term describes the solidification of metal in a mold during casting?
   A) Fusion
   B) Coagulation
   C) Crystallization
   D) Diffusion

15. Which material property is evaluated using a Brinell hardness test?
   A) Elasticity
   B) Surface hardness
   C) Fracture toughness
   D) Thermal expansion

16. Which process is used to shape materials by forcing them through a die under pressure?
   A) Casting
   B) Extrusion
   C) Forging
   D) Milling

17. Which material is typically used for high-temperature applications due to its low thermal expansion?
   A) Aluminum
   B) Ceramics
   C) Steel
   D) Polymers

18. What is the primary purpose of annealing metal?
   A) Increase hardness
   B) Improve ductility
   C) Enhance fatigue resistance
   D) Reduce melting point

19. Which material property is key for designing components subject to cyclic loading?
   A) Thermal conductivity
   B) Fatigue strength
   C) Elastic modulus
   D) Shear strength

20. What is the primary advantage of powder metallurgy over traditional manufacturing methods?
   A) Improved material ductility
   B) Lower production costs
   C) Ability to form complex shapes
   D) Enhanced surface hardness

21. Which of the following materials would be most suitable for an application requiring both excellent corrosion resistance and high strength at elevated temperatures?
   A) Aluminum Alloy 6061
   B) Stainless Steel 316
   C) Copper
   D) Titanium Alloy Ti-6Al-4V

22. In the powder metallurgy process, what is the purpose of the sintering step?
   A) To bind the powder particles together through heating
   B) To remove impurities from the powder
   C) To compact the powder into a desired shape
   D) To coat the particles with a protective layer

23. Which material property is most important for designing components subject to sudden impacts?
   A) Toughness
   B) Hardness
   C) Ductility
   D) Elasticity

24. Which casting defect is caused by rapid cooling leading to incomplete filling of the mold?
   A) Porosity
   B) Cold Shut
   C) Shrinkage Cavity
   D) Misrun

25. What type of crystal structure is typically associated with materials that exhibit excellent ductility?
   A) Body-Centered Cubic (BCC)
   B) Face-Centered Cubic (FCC)
   C) Hexagonal Close-Packed (HCP)
   D) Amorphous

26. Which surface treatment process uses a high-energy laser beam to improve the wear resistance of a component?
   A) Laser Hardening
   B) Case Hardening
   C) Plasma Nitriding
   D) Shot Peening

27. What is the primary factor that determines the fatigue strength of a material?
   A) Surface finish
   B) Thermal conductivity
   C) Hardness
   D) Density

28. Which type of heat treatment involves heating a material to a critical temperature, soaking, and slow cooling to improve machinability?
   A) Annealing
   B) Normalizing
   C) Quenching
   D) Tempering

29. What is the key difference between thermoplastics and thermosetting plastics when subjected to heat?
   A) Thermoplastics soften while thermosetting plastics harden
   B) Thermoplastics decompose while thermosetting plastics melt
   C) Thermoplastics can be remolded, while thermosetting plastics cannot
   D) Thermoplastics become brittle, while thermosetting plastics become elastic

30. Which manufacturing process is most suitable for creating complex hollow shapes in metals?
   A) Forging
   B) Extrusion
   C) Deep Drawing
   D) Investment Casting

31. Which property of a material is determined by its resistance to plastic deformation under load?
   A) Hardness
   B) Elastic Modulus
   C) Yield Strength
   D) Toughness

32. Laser cutting is a commonly used material processing method. Which of the following materials is best suited for this process?
   A) Aluminum
   B) Stainless Steel
   C) Lead
   D) Rubber

33. Which of the following is the most appropriate description of the term 'anisotropy' in materials?
   A) The material's properties are the same in all directions
   B) The material's properties vary with direction
   C) The material's properties change over time
   D) The material's properties improve after heat treatment

34. What is the primary purpose of cold rolling in metal processing?
   A) To heat metal to improve ductility
   B) To refine grain structure and improve surface finish
   C) To remove impurities from the metal surface
   D) To relieve residual stresses from the forging process

35. Which material property is essential for a component used in high-temperature furnace linings?
   A) Low thermal conductivity
   B) High thermal expansion
   C) High melting point
   D) Low density

36. Which metal forming process involves forcing material through a die to create objects of a fixed cross-sectional profile?
   A) Forging
   B) Extrusion
   C) Casting
   D) Milling

37. If a material exhibits a noticeable time-dependent strain under constant stress, it is said to experience which phenomenon?
   A) Elasticity
   B) Viscosity
   C) Creep
   D) Plastic deformation

38. What is the primary purpose of carburizing in surface hardening processes?
   A) To reduce the brittleness of the material
   B) To increase the carbon content at the surface
   C) To improve the corrosion resistance of the material
   D) To remove impurities from the surface

39. Which of the following describes the behavior of a viscoelastic material?
   A) It exhibits purely elastic deformation
   B) It exhibits both elastic and viscous behavior
   C) It exhibits purely plastic deformation
   D) It deforms permanently under low stresses

40. Which of the following is a key advantage of die casting over sand casting?
   A) Lower initial tooling costs
   B) Higher dimensional accuracy
   C) Ability to cast ferrous metals
   D) Lower operational temperature

41. What is the primary purpose of tempering steel after quenching?
   A) To increase hardness and reduce brittleness
   B) To improve ductility and reduce residual stresses
   C) To achieve full annealing
   D) To increase the material's density

42. Which of the following material processing methods is best suited for producing intricate, net-shaped components with minimal waste?
   A) Sand casting
   B) Powder metallurgy
   C) Hot rolling
   D) Extrusion

43. Which phenomenon is described by the tendency of a material to fracture due to prolonged exposure to cyclic loading below its ultimate tensile strength?
   A) Fatigue failure
   B) Creep
   C) Stress relaxation
   D) Yielding

44. During metal forming, which process involves shaping a material by rotating it on a lathe while applying pressure with a tool?
   A) Forging
   B) Spinning
   C) Extrusion
   D) Rolling

100. Which manufacturing process involves the use of a rotating tool to progressively remove material from a workpiece, primarily for creating cylindrical parts?
   A) Milling
   B) Turning
   C) Grinding
   D) Drilling



--- CORRECT ANSWERS AND EXPLANATIONS ---

1. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Yield strength is the maximum stress a material can endure before undergoing permanent deformation. It is crucial for applications requiring high load-bearing capacity.

2. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Quenching involves rapid cooling after heating, which creates a hard and brittle microstructure like martensite.

3. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Creep is the slow and progressive deformation of a material when subjected to a constant load over time, especially at high temperatures.

4. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: Refining is the process of purifying molten metal to remove impurities and achieve desired material properties.

5. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Ductility refers to the ability of a material to deform plastically before fracturing, making it ideal for applications like wire drawing.

6. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: Machining involves removing material from a workpiece using tools to achieve precise dimensions and finishes.

7. Correct Answer: D
   Explanation: Polymer-based composites, especially carbon-fiber-reinforced ones, exhibit exceptionally high tensile strength compared to metals.

8. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: Forging is a manufacturing process where metal is compressed and shaped by pressing between dies to achieve desired geometry.

9. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: The Charpy test measures the amount of energy absorbed by a material during fracture, which indicates its impact strength.

10. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Friction stir welding produces high-strength, defect-free welds, making it ideal for structural applications.

11. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: Surface roughness affects the initiation of cracks under cyclic loading, significantly influencing fatigue life.

12. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Stress relieving heats the material below its recrystallization temperature and cools it slowly, reducing internal stresses without changing the microstructure.

13. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: Polymers exhibit viscoelastic behavior, combining both viscous and elastic responses under deformation.

14. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: Crystallization refers to the formation of a solid structure as molten metal cools and solidifies in the mold.

15. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: The Brinell hardness test measures the material's resistance to indentation, indicating its surface hardness.

16. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Extrusion involves pushing material through a shaped die to create products like pipes and profiles.

17. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Ceramics have low thermal expansion and high thermal stability, making them ideal for high-temperature applications.

18. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Annealing involves heating and slow cooling to improve ductility and reduce brittleness by altering the microstructure.

19. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Fatigue strength determines how well a material can withstand cyclic loading without failure, making it crucial for such applications.

20. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: Powder metallurgy allows the creation of intricate shapes and complex geometries that are difficult to achieve with conventional manufacturing methods.

21. Correct Answer: D
   Explanation: Titanium Alloy Ti-6Al-4V has excellent corrosion resistance and retains strength at elevated temperatures, making it ideal for aerospace and chemical applications.

22. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: Sintering involves heating the compacted powder below its melting point to bond the particles together, enhancing the strength and integrity of the material.

23. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: Toughness is a material's ability to absorb energy and deform plastically without fracturing, making it crucial in impact resistance.

24. Correct Answer: D
   Explanation: Misrun occurs when the molten metal solidifies prematurely due to rapid cooling, resulting in incomplete filling of the mold.

25. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: FCC structures, such as those found in aluminum and copper, provide more slip systems, allowing for excellent ductility.

26. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: Laser hardening involves using a laser to quickly heat the material's surface, followed by rapid cooling, improving wear resistance.

27. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: Surface finish significantly affects fatigue strength, as smoother surfaces reduce stress concentrations where fatigue cracks can initiate.

28. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: Annealing improves machinability and reduces hardness by relieving internal stresses through heating and slow cooling.

29. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: Thermoplastics can be repeatedly melted and remolded, whereas thermosetting plastics cannot be remolded after curing due to their cross-linked structure.

30. Correct Answer: D
   Explanation: Investment casting involves creating a wax pattern coated in ceramic, which is burned out to form a mold for producing complex hollow shapes.

31. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: Hardness measures a material's resistance to plastic deformation, often determined through indentation or scratch testing.

32. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Stainless steel is suited for laser cutting due to its uniform texture and reflectivity, which enable precision cuts.

33. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Anisotropy refers to directional dependence of a material's properties, often observed in materials like wood or composites.

34. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Cold rolling refines the grain structure, enhances strength, and provides a better surface finish compared to hot rolling.

35. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: Materials used in high-temperature furnace linings need a high melting point to withstand extreme thermal conditions without degrading.

36. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Extrusion is a process where material is pushed through a die to produce objects with a consistent cross-section.

37. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: Creep refers to the slow, time-dependent deformation of a material under constant stress, typically occurring at high temperatures.

38. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Carburizing increases the carbon content at the surface, creating a hardened outer layer while maintaining a tough core.

39. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Viscoelastic materials combine elastic and viscous behavior, meaning they can recover their shape over time but also exhibit time-dependent strain.

40. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Die casting provides higher dimensional accuracy and smoother surface finishes compared to sand casting, making it ideal for mass production.

41. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Tempering is performed after quenching to reduce brittleness and improve the ductility of steel by relieving internal stresses caused by rapid cooling.

42. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Powder metallurgy is used to produce intricate net-shaped components with high material utilization and minimal waste.

43. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: Fatigue failure occurs when a material fractures due to repeated cyclic loading over time, even if the stress levels are below the ultimate tensile strength.

44. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Spinning is a metal forming process that uses a lathe to rotate the material while applying pressure with a tool to achieve the desired shape.

45. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Alloys are combinations of metals (and sometimes non-metals) that improve mechanical and chemical properties, such as strength, corrosion resistance, and hardness, compared to pure metals.

46. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: Galvanizing is a process in which steel is dipped into molten zinc to coat the surface, providing enhanced corrosion resistance.

47. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: Toughness is the measure of a material's ability to absorb energy and deform plastically before it fractures.

48. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Shot peening is used to increase surface hardness and fatigue strength by introducing compressive residual stresses on the surface.

49. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: Compressive strength measures the ability of a material to resist deformation or failure under an applied compressive force.

50. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Selective laser sintering (SLS) is an additive manufacturing process that uses a laser to selectively melt powder layers to create complex 3D objects.

51. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Fracture toughness is the property that describes a material's ability to resist crack propagation when under stress.

52. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Normalizing is a heat treatment process performed to refine the grain structure of a material and relieve internal stresses, improving overall mechanical properties.

53. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: The Brinell hardness test is a method for determining a material's resistance to surface indentation by pressing a hard sphere into the surface.

54. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: Nickel-based superalloys are specifically engineered to maintain strength, resist oxidation, and exhibit good creep resistance at high temperatures, making them ideal for gas turbine applications.

55. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: A riser serves as a reservoir of molten metal that compensates for shrinkage during solidification, ensuring that the casting is free from voids and defects.

56. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Tempering involves heating the steel to a temperature below its critical point to reduce brittleness and improve toughness while retaining most of the hardness achieved during quenching.

57. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: The Charpy impact test measures the toughness of a material by determining its ability to absorb energy during fracture at high strain rates.

58. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Powder metallurgy is ideal for forming complex ceramic parts because it allows precise control over the shape and material properties through pressing and sintering of ceramic powders.

59. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Fatigue strength is the ability of a material to withstand repeated loading and unloading cycles without failure, making it crucial for cyclic loading applications.

60. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Electric discharge machining (EDM) uses electrical discharges (sparks) to remove material from electrically conductive workpieces, making it suitable for hard materials and complex shapes.

61. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: Ceramics typically have a high modulus of elasticity, indicating stiffness, and low tensile ductility, meaning they are brittle and prone to fracture under tensile stress.

62. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: Hot rolling improves the workability of metals by reducing their strength and increasing ductility at elevated temperatures, making it easier to shape and form.

63. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Elasticity is the property of a material that allows it to return to its original shape after the removal of a deforming force, as long as the stress is within the elastic limit.

64. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Case hardening focuses on increasing the surface hardness of a material to improve wear resistance while maintaining a ductile core for overall toughness.

65. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Hardness measures a material's resistance to localized plastic deformation, commonly assessed through indentation tests like Brinell, Rockwell, or Vickers.

66. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: Additives in polymer extrusion are used to modify properties such as flexibility, UV resistance, flame retardancy, and color, allowing customization for specific applications.

67. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: Creep is the tendency of a material to deform progressively under a constant load over time, typically at high temperatures relative to the material's melting point.

68. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Blow molding is ideal for producing hollow plastic parts, as it uses air pressure to expand molten plastic into the shape of a mold cavity.

69. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: Toughness is the material's ability to absorb energy and deform plastically without fracturing, making it essential for components exposed to high-speed impacts.

70. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: Shot peening improves fatigue strength by creating compressive residual stresses on the surface, which prevent crack initiation and propagation under cyclic loading.

71. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Composite materials offer a high strength-to-weight ratio due to their low density, making them ideal for aerospace applications where weight reduction is critical.

72. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: Friction welding uses heat generated by mechanical friction and compressive force to achieve solid-state bonding between two metal surfaces.

73. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: Ductile metals exhibit a yield point where plastic deformation begins, followed by strain hardening and necking before eventual fracture.

74. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Surface finish plays a key role in fatigue life because surface imperfections can act as stress concentration points where cracks initiate during cyclic loading.

75. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Argon is commonly used as a shielding gas in GTAW for aluminum because it provides excellent arc stability and prevents oxidation of the weld.

76. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: The Rockwell hardness test measures the depth of penetration of a steel ball or cone under load, making it suitable for rapid and repeatable testing.

77. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Carbon is added to steel to increase its hardness and strength by forming hard carbide phases within the iron matrix.

78. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Investment casting, also known as lost-wax casting, is known for producing parts with high dimensional accuracy and excellent surface finish.

79. Correct Answer: D
   Explanation: Creep resistance is essential for materials used in turbine blades because it ensures the material maintains its shape and mechanical properties under sustained high temperatures and stresses.

80. Correct Answer: D
   Explanation: Deep drawing is a metal forming process in which a sheet metal blank is radially drawn into a forming die by the mechanical action of a punch to create complex shapes.

81. Correct Answer: D
   Explanation: The compact tension test is a standard method used to measure the fracture toughness of a material by evaluating its resistance to crack propagation.

82. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: Stereolithography (SLA) uses a UV laser to selectively cure liquid photopolymer resin layer by layer, creating high-resolution 3D parts.

83. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: Invar is an alloy with an exceptionally low coefficient of thermal expansion, making it ideal for precision applications where dimensional stability is critical.

84. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: Resistivity is the key property that determines a material's ability to conduct electricity. Materials with low resistivity, such as copper, are excellent conductors.

85. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: Physical vapor deposition (PVD) involves evaporating material in a vacuum chamber, which then condenses onto the substrate to form a thin coating.

86. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: Poisson's ratio is the ratio of lateral strain to axial strain in a material subjected to tensile or compressive stress.

87. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Closed-die forging involves enclosing the metal workpiece entirely within a die, allowing complex shapes to be formed with high precision.

88. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: Pitting corrosion is a localized form of corrosion that results in small holes or pits on the material surface, often caused by chloride ions in the environment.

89. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Aluminum and many ductile metals exhibit significant plastic deformation before failure, making them suitable for forming and shaping processes.

90. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Annealing is used to relieve internal stresses, improve ductility, and restore the material's mechanical properties by heating it to a specific temperature and then cooling slowly.

91. Correct Answer: D
   Explanation: Anisotropy refers to the directional dependence of material properties, often caused by the alignment of grains during processes such as rolling.

92. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: Brazing uses a filler metal with a melting point above 450°C but lower than the base metals to join components without melting the base materials.

93. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: Hardness is critical for cutting tools because it determines their ability to resist wear and deformation when machining hard materials.

94. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Elasticity is the ability of a material to deform under stress and return to its original shape once the stress is removed.

95. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Copper-nickel alloys offer high thermal conductivity and superior corrosion resistance in marine environments, making them an ideal choice for such applications.

96. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: Normalizing involves heating a material to a higher temperature and then air cooling it to refine the grain structure, enhancing mechanical properties like toughness and strength.

97. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: Low toughness indicates that the material cannot absorb much energy before fracturing. Brittle materials typically fail without significant plastic deformation.

98. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Stress relieving is a heat treatment process used to reduce internal stresses without significantly affecting the material's hardness or strength.

99. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Fatigue strength is the ability of a material to withstand cyclic loading without failure, making it a critical property for components subjected to repetitive stress.

100. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Turning is a machining process that uses a lathe to remove material from a rotating workpiece, commonly used to produce cylindrical components.


FE MECHANICAL – Fluid Mechanics

1. A rectangular gate is submerged vertically in water. The top edge of the gate is 2 m below the water surface, and the gate measures 3 m wide by 4 m high. What is the magnitude of the resultant hydrostatic force acting on the gate?
   A) 118.8 kN
   B) 235.2 kN
   C) 176.4 kN
   D) 294.0 kN

2. A pipe carrying water experiences a sudden contraction from a diameter of 0.3 m to 0.15 m. If water enters the larger section at 2 m/s, what is the velocity at the smaller section?
   A) 4 m/s
   B) 8 m/s
   C) 6 m/s
   D) 2 m/s

3. A fluid flows through a horizontal pipe that narrows from a diameter of 0.5 m to 0.25 m. The pressure at the wider section is 150 kPa, and the velocity is 3 m/s. Assuming incompressible flow, what is the pressure at the narrower section?
   A) 90.5 kPa
   B) 100.2 kPa
   C) 112.3 kPa
   D) 125.7 kPa

4. A fluid with a viscosity of 0.001 Pa·s flows through a pipe of diameter 0.1 m. If the velocity profile is parabolic and the maximum velocity at the center is 4 m/s, what is the average velocity?
   A) 1.33 m/s
   B) 2 m/s
   C) 2.67 m/s
   D) 3 m/s

5. Using the Buckingham π theorem, determine the number of dimensionless π groups that can be formed for the relationship of Reynolds number, considering the variables: velocity (V), characteristic length (L), density (ρ), and viscosity (μ).
   A) 3
   B) 2
   C) 1
   D) 4

6. In a turbulent pipe flow, the friction factor (f) is found using the Moody chart. If the Reynolds number is 15,000 and the relative roughness is 0.001, what is the approximate friction factor?
   A) 0.016
   B) 0.02
   C) 0.018
   D) 0.014

7. A rectangular channel has a width of 3 m and carries water at a depth of 2 m. If the flow rate is 30 m³/s, what is the average velocity of flow?
   A) 3 m/s
   B) 4 m/s
   C) 5 m/s
   D) 2.5 m/s

8. A centrifugal pump operates at 1500 rpm and delivers a flow rate of 0.1 m³/s against a head of 20 m. The shaft power input is 10 kW. What is the pump efficiency?
   A) 20%
   B) 50%
   C) 70%
   D) 80%

9. A cylindrical storage tank with a diameter of 10 m is filled with water to a height of 8 m. What is the absolute pressure in kPa at the bottom of the tank? Assume atmospheric pressure is 101.3 kPa and the density of water is 1000 kg/m³.
   A) 108.2 kPa
   B) 179.3 kPa
   C) 178.3 kPa
   D) 120.3 kPa

10. Water flows steadily through a horizontal Venturi meter. The inlet diameter is 0.4 m, and the throat diameter is 0.2 m. If the pressure difference between the inlet and throat is 20 kPa, what is the flow rate? Assume the density of water is 1000 kg/m³.
   A) 0.126 m³/s
   B) 0.157 m³/s
   C) 0.182 m³/s
   D) 0.200 m³/s

11. A liquid has a dynamic viscosity of 0.5 Pa·s and a kinematic viscosity of 0.0005 m²/s. What is the density of the liquid in kg/m³?
   A) 500 kg/m³
   B) 1000 kg/m³

   B) 3 m²
   C) 4 m²
   D) 5 m²

119. A spherical particle with a diameter of 0.001 m is settling in water under Stokes flow conditions. The density of the particle is 2500 kg/m³, the density of water is 1000 kg/m³, and the dynamic viscosity of water is 0.001 Pa·s. What is the terminal settling velocity?
   A) 0.01 m/s
   B) 0.02 m/s
   C) 0.03 m/s
   D) 0.04 m/s

120. A converging nozzle has an inlet diameter of 0.1 m and an outlet diameter of 0.05 m. The inlet velocity is 5 m/s. What is the velocity at the outlet?
   A) 10 m/s
   B) 15 m/s
   C) 20 m/s
   D) 25 m/s



--- CORRECT ANSWERS AND EXPLANATIONS ---

1. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: The hydrostatic force is calculated as F = ρghA. The depth to the center of pressure is 2 m + (4 m/2) = 4 m. Using ρ = 1000 kg/m³, g = 9.81 m/s², and A = 3 × 4 = 12 m², the force is F = (1000)(9.81)(4)(12) = 176.4 kN.

2. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Using the principle of continuity, A₁v₁ = A₂v₂. The area of the larger pipe is A₁ = π(0.3/2)² = 0.0707 m², and the area of the smaller pipe is A₂ = π(0.15/2)² = 0.0177 m². Solving for v₂ gives v₂ = A₁v₁/A₂ = (0.0707 × 2) / 0.0177 = 8 m/s.

3. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: Apply Bernoulli's equation: P₁ + 0.5ρv₁² = P₂ + 0.5ρv₂². First, find v₂ using continuity: v₂ = (A₁v₁)/A₂. A₁ = π(0.5/2)² = 0.196 m² and A₂ = π(0.25/2)² = 0.049 m². So, v₂ = (0.196 × 3) / 0.049 = 12 m/s. Substitute into Bernoulli's equation: 150,000 + 0.5(1000)(3)² = P₂ + 0.5(1000)(12)². Solve for P₂: P₂ = 90,500 Pa = 90.5 kPa.

4. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: For laminar flow in a circular pipe, the average velocity is half the maximum velocity. Hence, the average velocity is v_avg = v_max / 2 = 4 / 2 = 2 m/s.

5. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: The number of dimensionless groups is given by the formula n - r, where n is the number of variables, and r is the number of fundamental dimensions. Here, n = 4 and r = 3 (M, L, T). Thus, there are 4 - 3 = 1 dimensionless group, and that group represents the Reynolds number.

6. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: From the Moody chart, for Re = 15,000 and a relative roughness of 0.001, the friction factor f is approximately 0.016.

7. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: The flow rate Q is given by Q = A × v, where A is the cross-sectional area. For a rectangular channel, A = width × depth = 3 × 2 = 6 m². Solve for v: v = Q / A = 30 / 6 = 5 m/s.

8. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: The pump efficiency is η = (ρgQH) / P. Using ρ = 1000 kg/m³, g = 9.81 m/s², Q = 0.1 m³/s, H = 20 m, and P = 10,000 W, η = [(1000)(9.81)(0.1)(20)] / 10,000 = 0.70 = 70%.

9. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: The pressure at the bottom of the tank is the sum of the atmospheric pressure and the hydrostatic pressure. Hydrostatic pressure = ρgh = (1000)(9.81)(8) = 78.48 kPa. Adding atmospheric pressure, total pressure = 101.3 + 78.48 = 178.3 kPa.

10. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: Using the Bernoulli equation and continuity, the flow rate can be calculated as Q = A₁A₂√(2ΔP/ρ)/(√(A₁² - A₂²)), where A₁ = π(0.4/2)², A₂ = π(0.2/2)², ΔP = 20,000 Pa, and ρ = 1000 kg/m³. Substituting values gives Q ≈ 0.126 m³/s.

11. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: The density of the fluid can be calculated as ρ = μ/ν, where μ is the dynamic viscosity and ν is the kinematic viscosity. Substituting values: ρ = 0.5 / 0.0005 = 1000 kg/m³.

12. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: The power output is given by P = ρgQHη, where ρ = 1000 kg/m³, g = 9.81 m/s², Q = 0.3 m³/s, H = 50 m, and η = 0.85. Substituting values: P = (1000)(9.81)(0.3)(50)(0.85) ≈ 150 kW.

13. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: The hydraulic radius is R = A/P, where A is the cross-sectional area and P is the wetted perimeter. A = b*d + z*d² = 4*3 + 2*3² = 24 m². P = b + 2√(1+z²)*d = 4 + 2√(1+4)*3 ≈ 13.3 m. R = 24 / 13.3 ≈ 1.8 m.

14. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: There are 5 variables (F, V, D, ρ, μ) and 3 fundamental dimensions (M, L, T). Therefore, the number of π groups is 5 - 3 = 2.

15. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: For incompressible flow, the divergence of the velocity field must be zero. ∇·V = ∂(2x)/∂x + ∂(3y)/∂y + ∂(4z)/∂z = 2 + 3 + 4 ≠ 0. Thus, the flow is compressible.

16. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: The equivalent resistance for parallel pipes is given by 1/R_eq = 1/R₁ + 1/R₂ + 1/R₃. Substituting values: 1/R_eq = 1/5 + 1/10 + 1/15 ≈ 0.3. R_eq = 1/0.3 ≈ 3.33.

17. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: The force due to viscous drag can be approximated for laminar flow as F = μUWL, where μ = 0.02 Pa.s, U = 4 m/s, W = 1 m, L = 2 m. F = 0.02 × 4 × 2 × 1 = 1.28 N.

   Explanation: The critical Reynolds number for transition is approximately 5 × 10⁵. Since the given value exceeds this but is not extremely high, the flow is in the transition regime.

118. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: The cross-sectional area is calculated as A = (b + z*h)h, where b = 2 m, z = 1, and h = 1 m. Substituting the values gives A = 3 m².

119. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: Using Stokes' law, the terminal velocity is calculated as V = (2/9)(ρp - ρf)g(d²/μ). Substituting the given values gives 0.01 m/s.

120. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: Using the continuity equation A1V1 = A2V2, the outlet velocity is calculated as 20 m/s.

FE MECHANICAL – Thermodynamics

1. A closed system undergoes a process where 500 kJ of heat is added to the system and 200 kJ of work is done by the system. What is the change in internal energy of the system?
   A) 300 kJ
   B) 700 kJ
   C) -300 kJ
   D) 500 kJ

2. Which of the following statements about the Second Law of Thermodynamics is correct?
   A) It states that energy cannot be created or destroyed.
   B) It states that the entropy of a closed system always decreases.
   C) It states that heat cannot spontaneously flow from a colder body to a hotter body.
   D) It states that work output is always greater than heat input.

3. A piston-cylinder device contains 2 kg of water at 150°C and is heated until the temperature reaches 300°C. Assuming constant pressure, what phase is the water at 300°C?
   A) Compressed liquid
   B) Saturated liquid
   C) Superheated vapor
   D) Saturated vapor

4. An ideal gas at a pressure of 100 kPa, a volume of 2 m³, and a temperature of 300 K is compressed isothermally to half its initial volume. What is the final pressure of the gas?
   A) 100 kPa
   B) 150 kPa
   C) 200 kPa
   D) 300 kPa

5. A 5 kg block of aluminum (c = 900 J/kg·K) is heated from 25°C to 75°C. How much heat is required?
   A) 112,500 J
   B) 225,000 J
   C) 450,000 J
   D) 90,000 J

6. Which of the following processes will result in an increase in entropy?
   A) Condensation of steam
   B) Freezing of water
   C) Expansion of gas in a vacuum
   D) Compression of an ideal gas

   A) Pump
   B) Boiler
   C) Turbine
   D) Condenser

   A) 50 kJ
   B) 100 kJ
   C) 150 kJ
   D) 200 kJ

   A) Efficiency decreases
   B) Efficiency increases
   C) Efficiency remains constant

   B) 0.3
   C) 0.4
   D) 0.6

   A) 450 K
   B) 600 K
   C) 800 K
   D) 400 K

   A) 30%
   B) 50%
   C) 60%
   D) 70%

   C) 603 kJ
   D) 1507.5 kJ

   B) A refrigerator extracts heat from a cold reservoir.
   C) A heat engine operates with 100% efficiency.

   B) Negative
   C) Zero
   D) Cannot be determined

   C) 800 kJ

169. A heat engine operating between a source at 1000 K and a sink at 300 K produces 200 kJ of work. What is the maximum possible efficiency of this engine?
   A) 30%
   B) 50%
   C) 70%
   D) 80%

170. A heat pump provides 10 kW of heating to a room. If the COP of the heat pump is 4, what is the electrical power input to the heat pump?
   A) 2.5 kW
   B) 4 kW
   C) 6 kW
   D) 8 kW



--- CORRECT ANSWERS AND EXPLANATIONS ---

1. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: The First Law of Thermodynamics states: ΔU = Q - W. Here, Q = 500 kJ and W = 200 kJ, so ΔU = 500 - 200 = 300 kJ.

2. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: The Second Law of Thermodynamics states that heat cannot spontaneously flow from a colder body to a hotter body without external work being applied.

3. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: At 300°C and constant pressure, water is in the superheated vapor phase as it is beyond the saturation temperature for the given pressure.

4. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: For isothermal processes, P1V1 = P2V2. P2 = P1V1/V2 = (100 kPa)(2 m³)/(1 m³) = 200 kPa.

5. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Heat required is Q = mcΔT. Here, m = 5 kg, c = 900 J/kg·K, ΔT = 75°C - 25°C = 50°C. Q = (5)(900)(50) = 225,000 J.

6. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: Entropy increases in processes involving greater molecular disorder, such as the expansion of gas in a vacuum.

7. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: The turbine in the Rankine cycle expands the steam, converting thermal energy into mechanical work.

8. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: COP = Qc/W. Rearrange to find W = Qc/COP. Here, Qc = 200 kJ, COP = 4. W = 200/4 = 50 kJ.

9. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Increasing the compression ratio raises the thermal efficiency of the Brayton cycle since efficiency depends on temperature ratios.

10. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: Mole fraction of oxygen = moles of oxygen / total moles = 2 / (2+3) = 2/5 = 0.4.

11. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: For an ideal gas in a rigid tank, the volume remains constant. Applying the ideal gas law (P1/T1 = P2/T2), solving for T2 gives T2 = (P2 * T1) / P1 = (400 kPa * 300 K) / 200 kPa = 600 K.

12. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: The maximum efficiency of a reversible engine is given by the Carnot efficiency: η = 1 - (T_sink / T_source). Substituting the values: η = 1 - (300 K / 600 K) = 0.5 or 50%.

13. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: Entropy change = Q/T_hot - Q/T_cold. Substituting: ΔS = (10 kW / (90°C + 273)) - (10 kW / (20°C + 273)) ≈ 0.037 kW/K.

14. Correct Answer: D
   Explanation: The work done during a gas compression or expansion is calculated using W = ∫ P dv. Assuming polytropic compression, integrate the pressure-volume relationship to find work.

15. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: The heat transfer is calculated using Q = m * Cp * ΔT. Substituting: Q = 1 kg * 1.005 kJ/kg·K * (600 K - 300 K) = 603 kJ.

16. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: The Second Law of Thermodynamics states no engine can be 100% efficient because some energy must be rejected to the surroundings.

17. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: Using steam tables, locate the entropy at the initial condition and match it to the final pressure to find the final temperature.

18. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: The thermal efficiency of an Otto cycle increases with an increase in compression ratio according to η = 1 - (1/r^(γ-1)), where r = compression ratio.

19. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: COP = T_evap / (T_cond - T_evap) when temperatures are in Kelvin. Substituting: COP = (263 K) / (313 K - 263 K) ≈ 3.0.

20. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: During combustion, heat is generated and entropy typically increases due to the irreversibility of the process.

21. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: The change in internal energy is calculated using the First Law of Thermodynamics: ΔU = Q - W. Substituting Q = 500 kJ and W = 300 kJ, we get ΔU = 500 - 300 = 200 kJ.

22. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: The power output is calculated using the specific enthalpy difference between inlet and outlet states: W = ṁ(h_in - h_out). Thermodynamic tables provide h_in and h_out at specified states.

23. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: Using the ideal gas law and considering constant volume, the pressure is proportional to the temperature. P_final = P_initial × (T_final / T_initial). Substituting values: P_final = 300 × (600 / 400) = 450 kPa.

24. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: Entropy is defined as a measure of disorder or randomness in a system, and it increases in irreversible processes.

25. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: The efficiency of a Carnot engine is η = 1 - (T_low / T_high). Work output is η × Q_in. Substituting values: η = 1 - (300 / 500) = 0.4; Work output = 0.4 × 600 = 240 kJ.

26. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: For an ideal gas, internal energy depends only on temperature. In an isothermal process, the temperature remains constant, so internal energy does not change.

27. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: The equation PV = constant describes an isothermal process, where temperature remains constant throughout the expansion or compression.

28. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: A pump is used to increase the pressure of incompressible fluids, such as liquids, without significantly increasing temperature.

29. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: Gibbs free energy determines the maximum amount of work that can be extracted from a system at constant temperature and pressure.

30. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Reheating the steam increases the average temperature at which heat is added, leading to improved thermal efficiency of the cycle.

31. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Using the ideal gas law, PV = mRT. The mass of air can be calculated for the initial and final states, given constant pressure and change in temperature.

32. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: The COP is defined as COP = Q/W. Rearranging gives W = Q/COP. Substituting Q = 12 kW and COP = 3, W = 4 kW.

33. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: The condenser’s role in the Rankine cycle is to cool the steam and convert it into liquid water to facilitate pumping back to the boiler.

34. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: In an adiabatic process, there is no heat transfer. The temperature increases when the pressure increases if the gas is compressed.

35. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: An isentropic process is a reversible adiabatic process. For ideal gases, n = γ (the ratio of specific heats Cp/Cv).

36. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: The velocity increase implies conversion of enthalpy into kinetic energy, resulting in a decrease in specific enthalpy.

37. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: The Gibbs free energy defines the maximum reversible work obtainable from a system under constant temperature and pressure.

38. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: The process PV = constant corresponds to an isothermal process for an ideal gas since temperature remains constant.

39. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: The maximum thermal efficiency for a Carnot engine is given by η = 1 - (T_low / T_high). Substituting values, η = 1 - (300/800) = 62.5%.

40. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: As heat is added to the rigid tank, the steam remains superheated. No phase change occurs because the substance remains in the superheated region.

41. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: Using the Carnot efficiency formula, η = 1 - (T_low/T_high). The efficiency is 0.5, meaning 50% of the heat absorbed is converted to work. The rejected heat is therefore equal to the work produced (200 kJ) divided by 0.5, giving 400 kJ.

42. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Heat transfer through a finite temperature difference involves entropy generation, making the process irreversible.

43. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: Heat required in a constant volume process is calculated using Q = m * Cv * ΔT. Substituting, Q = 1 * 0.717 * (400 - 300) = 143.4 kJ.

44. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: Using the First Law of Thermodynamics: ΔU = Q - W. Substituting, ΔU = 600 - 150 = 450 kJ.

45. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: The entropy change of the surroundings is -100/300 = -0.333 kJ/K. The total entropy change is 20 - 0.333 = 19.667 kJ/K, which is positive and complies with the Second Law.

46. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Entropy generation can be calculated as Q*(1/T_sink - 1/T_source). Substituting, S_gen = 200*(1/313 - 1/383) ≈ 1.0 kW/K.

47. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: At 45°C, the saturation pressure of water is approximately 10 kPa, which is the pressure in the condenser for saturated liquid.

48. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Work done in an isothermal process is calculated using W = nRT * ln(V2/V1). Substituting the pressure-volume relationship gives W = P1V1 * ln(V2/V1) ≈ 41.4 kJ.

49. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: For an adiabatic process, T2/T1 = (V1/V2)^(γ-1). Using γ = 1.4 for air, T2 = 500 * (1/2)^(0.4) ≈ 400 K.

50. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: Efficiency of a Brayton cycle increases with the pressure ratio according to η = 1 - (T_low/T_high)*(P_low/P_high)^(γ-1/γ).

51. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: For a rigid tank, the volume is constant. Using the ideal gas law, the pressure is directly proportional to the temperature when volume is constant. Doubling the temperature doubles the pressure: (100 kPa)(600 K / 300 K) = 200 kPa.

52. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: The maximum efficiency for a heat engine is determined by the Carnot efficiency: η = 1 - (T_cold / T_hot). Substituting the values, η = 1 - (300/700) = 0.571 = 57.1%.

53. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: Since the turbine operates adiabatically and no irreversibilities are mentioned, the process is isentropic, meaning there is no change in specific entropy.

54. Correct Answer: C
